  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

    };

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2360699629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5455886540165786292"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>If curiosity killed the cat, it was satisfaction that brought it back.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>This is one of those rare few books that really shows me why we need a 3 1/2 star rating, and I don’t like to give 1/2 stars. This… was so fun, and a four star book for me, and also it bugged the shit out of me to the point where I texted someone to bitch about it. But… I honestly did have so much fun.<br/><br/>Let’s get the complaining out of the way: <b>
  <u>god, I fucking hate 2004 YA.</u>
</b> I mean, this text has a bunch of homopho</span>
  <span id="freeText5455886540165786292" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>If curiosity killed the cat, it was satisfaction that brought it back.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />This is one of those rare few books that really shows me why we need a 3 1/2 star rating, and I don’t like to give 1/2 stars. This… was so fun, and a four star book for me, and also it bugged the shit out of me to the point where I texted someone to bitch about it. But… I honestly did have so much fun.<br /><br />Let’s get the complaining out of the way: <b>
  <u>god, I fucking hate 2004 YA.</u>
</b> I mean, this text has a bunch of homophobia and racism in there for “realism,” and yet somehow it still managed to sound like How No Teen Talks Ever. Everything that happens with Corny kind of pisses me off a lot. And some of how Kaye’s being biracial is introduced… rubbed me the wrong way? I can’t really figure out why. It just felt weird.<br /><br />BUT.<br /><br />So first of all, on the good side… <b>
  <u>the fairies</u>
</b>. The way Holly Black draws her fairy worlds and fairy characters is genuinely so imaginative, gorgeous, and… creepy. Every time I dive into one of her books, I find myself both terrified and enamored with her fairy world, and I am so okay with that.<br /><br />And more importantly, this is a very thematically strong book! There’s the fantastic meta-narrative about growing up, and learning to live with how others perceive you. There is no easy fix for Kaye’s life; no box to easily fit into. She is a member of the fairy world of the human world and she can’t figure out which one is which. <br /><br />Kaye, though, is <b>
  <u>a really unlikable lead.</u>
</b> I don’t mean that she’s flawed – though she is – I mean, I actively didn’t like her at all, and I love unlikable lady leads. I found that she was one of those early YA protagonists who’s written <i>just generic enough</i> that she’s easy to make into a self insert. <br /><br />She’s not... awful. But she’s very selfish. And not in a delicious way — in a way that’s really annoying because she keeps fucking up and the narrative doesn’t notice or criticize it. <br /><br />Oh, but I will admit - I fucking love Roiben. I really hate reading YA sometimes because inevitably, if there’s some male love interest that everyone fangirls over, the female lead will be unquestionably the best character in the narrative. [I mean, to mention another Holly Black book, The Cruel Prince?? some of you just don’t appreciate Jude like you should.] But no, Roiben is so incredibly likable and compelling. It’s a cliche trope, but I adore it when characters who keep up walls fall for characters who encourage them not to do so. I absolutely loved him.<br /><br />The main thing I want to say is that this is just… a really fun book. It's so short that I basically bingeread it and oh, loved it. And do you guys even understand how fucking short this book is? it's 320 pages but every page is like, in sixteen point font, and also half the size of a normal book page, and I'm honestly just confused as to how this is a full novel. This would be great for fans of any of Holly Black’s current books or anyone who just wants to read a really fun, trashy YA book with a gorgeous fairy world and a really good love interest. Hey, I liked it.<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a>⭐Look out for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2469917722" rel="nofollow noopener">my review of book two</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/283494.Ironside" rel="nofollow noopener">my review of book three</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5455886540165786292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_49538576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49538576" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/297700-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595109513p2/297700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49538576?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/297700-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/297700-shannon?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/297700-shannon?shelf=my-reviews">my-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/297700-shannon?shelf=home-library-read">home-library-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49538576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3134671529418146583">Read #4? probably<br/>Started on <b>June 4, 2019</b><br/>Finished on <b>June 5, 2019</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“If you would help me, draw this arrow." His eyes narrowed, and he shook his head. "If not, then push it in as deep as you can and hope it kills me.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Still a hoe for Kaye and Roiben and I'm not sorry about it<br/><br/>(<a href='https://twitter.com/feyspeaker/status/1132363156020269057' rel='nofollow noopener'>This masterpiece</a> made me do a re-read. My eyes will never be the same. Petition for more Kaye/Roiben fanart)<br/><br/>OG REVIEW THAT I'M STILL AMAZED SO PEOPLE HAVE LIKED SO *THANK YOU* IF YOU'RE ONE OF THEM<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560218994ra/27649009.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓<br/><br/>I'm going to be up </span>
  <span id="freeText3134671529418146583" style="display:none">Read #4? probably<br>Started on <b>June 4, 2019</b><br>Finished on <b>June 5, 2019</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“If you would help me, draw this arrow." His eyes narrowed, and he shook his head. "If not, then push it in as deep as you can and hope it kills me.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Still a hoe for Kaye and Roiben and I'm not sorry about it<br><br>(<a href="https://twitter.com/feyspeaker/status/1132363156020269057" rel="nofollow noopener">This masterpiece</a> made me do a re-read. My eyes will never be the same. Petition for more Kaye/Roiben fanart)<br><br>OG REVIEW THAT I'M STILL AMAZED SO PEOPLE HAVE LIKED SO *THANK YOU* IF YOU'RE ONE OF THEM<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560218994ra/27649009.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓<br><br>I'm going to be up front... this series? You will either love it or hate it. Personally, I absolutely love gritty real-life/fantasy stories when they're written well, and I think Holly Black does the combination so much freaking justice. It doesn't try too hard to be overly badass. Kaye is such a great lead -- although I don't always see myself in her actions throughout the book, I still liked her because she was <i>real</i>. I never got the sense that Holly Black was trying to impress me; she was just writing about a real girl. And honestly, when I compare female leads in other books, I always think about Kaye and if they live up to her standards (which is not often enough for me).<br><br>So many people cut down Tithe for its "objectionable" content, but I was actually able to find a lot of realism in the way most of the characters behaved. As I was growing up, the teenagers I knew cursed like sailors and were always trading stories about sex. Unfortunately or not, it's a way of life nowadays -- teenagers are naturally curious. I think in this case, Holly Black's choice to include these situations and words make her characters come alive. However, that's not all Tithe is about -- people want to focus on that, but it's only a small portion of the entire book. Tithe is different, and some people just don't enjoy or understand how YA can fit that profile. But that's the one thing I appreciate about Holly Black: her ability to take YA to another level. She proves that the genre doesn't have to be a complete trope-fest with beginnings and ends that fit together perfectly.<br><br>For me, Holly Black's writing in Tithe is really hard to pin down. It's like a combination of trippy and poetic. The way she describes things, you feel like you're reading poetry -- I love the detail she pours into Tithe. I think my favorite sections have to be when she describes the faeries and where they live -- she makes it all gothic-y and enchanting and it just makes me feel like I have a spell cast over me that forces me to be in this complete daze. I can't get out of it if I wanted to. I just keep reading every sentence she writes and loving them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3134671529418146583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_57724677" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57724677" />
    <a title="Julie Kagawa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2364898-julie-kagawa"><img alt="Julie Kagawa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257815866p2/2364898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/57724677?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie Kagawa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie Kagawa" href="/user/show/2364898-julie-kagawa">Julie Kagawa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer57724677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17249501347946806000">Tithe is a very raw, very dark faerie tale. While not suitable for younger readers (lots of swearing, random torture and violence, and mature themes), I loved its take on the darker side of faerie. It deals with faerie themes like Changelings and the knowing of one's True Name very well, and Roiben is probably my favorite faery hero of all time. (Kind of like Sephiroth. If you know who Sephiroth is, you'll understand.) <br/><br/>The writing was a teensy bit sporadic and hard to follow at first. I found my</span>
  <span id="freeText17249501347946806000" style="display:none">Tithe is a very raw, very dark faerie tale. While not suitable for younger readers (lots of swearing, random torture and violence, and mature themes), I loved its take on the darker side of faerie. It deals with faerie themes like Changelings and the knowing of one's True Name very well, and Roiben is probably my favorite faery hero of all time. (Kind of like Sephiroth. If you know who Sephiroth is, you'll understand.) <br /><br />The writing was a teensy bit sporadic and hard to follow at first. I found myself going back and re-reading passages to understand them. All-in-all, though, a great story for older, more mature audiences. By the time I got to its sequel, Ironside, I was hooked on Holly Black.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17249501347946806000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10720603246262116008">I was not expecting to be blown away by this and gosh am I so glad I kept my expectations low. <br/><br/>The main reason I read these books is because I absolutely loved <i>The Cruel Prince</i> and <i>The Wicked King</i>. And since I don't know what to do with myself while I wait for <i>The Queen of Nothing</i> I decided to get to know more about the other faerie courts which is set in the same world as TCP. <br/><br/><br/>Kaye thought that she was just an ordinary girl. When one day her friend mistakenly enters a faerie realm, things chang</span>
  <span id="freeText10720603246262116008" style="display:none">I was not expecting to be blown away by this and gosh am I so glad I kept my expectations low. <br /><br />The main reason I read these books is because I absolutely loved <i>The Cruel Prince</i> and <i>The Wicked King</i>. And since I don't know what to do with myself while I wait for <i>The Queen of Nothing</i> I decided to get to know more about the other faerie courts which is set in the same world as TCP. <br /><br /><br />Kaye thought that she was just an ordinary girl. When one day her friend mistakenly enters a faerie realm, things change for her. She discovers that she is not an ordinary, but one of the lesser faeries. A pixie to be exact. Her whole life has been a lie. And Kaye wants to know exactly how she came to live in the human realm disguised as a human without knowing her true nature. <br /><br /><br />The first half of <i>Tithe</i> was not very interesting. It was absolutely boring to be honest. But when (gorgeous) Roiben came into the picture I became more invested (*wink*). If it wasn't for Roiben I might have DNF-ed this, he made it worthwhile. <br />____<br /><i>Pre-Read</i><br />If you think the only reason I'm reading this book is because it's set in the same world as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2417729031" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cruel Prince</a> then you are <b>absolutely... <i>CORRECT</i>.</b> *ding! ding! ding!*</span>

<div id="review_203516553" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203516553" />
    <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru"><img alt="Tomoe Hotaru" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571221863p2/5548051.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203516553?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tomoe Hotaru" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru">Tomoe Hotaru</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=not-my-cuppa-tea">not-my-cuppa-tea</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=craptastic">craptastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=contemporary-fantasy">contemporary-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203516553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15103803975263501186">Ugh. I don't know where to start with this one so I'm gonna jump right in. I didn't like it. It was all just a raging bunch of WTF?! for me. I mean, it was random. My brain hurts so this isn't going to be a very coherent review.<br/><br/>Before I go to my detailed ravings, it's best if I gave a brief overview of what this book was about. It's the story of Kaye, a changeling, who was put under a glamour to hide her true green-skinned self and lives with her rockstar wannabe "mother", Ellen. Her life ultima</span>
  <span id="freeText15103803975263501186" style="display:none">Ugh. I don't know where to start with this one so I'm gonna jump right in. I didn't like it. It was all just a raging bunch of WTF?! for me. I mean, it was random. My brain hurts so this isn't going to be a very coherent review.<br><br>Before I go to my detailed ravings, it's best if I gave a brief overview of what this book was about. It's the story of Kaye, a changeling, who was put under a glamour to hide her true green-skinned self and lives with her rockstar wannabe "mother", Ellen. Her life ultimately changes when her mother was almost murdered in a <s>pathetic, lame excuse of an</s> attempted stabbing, and having nowhere else to go, they return to their home town.<br>Here, Kaye suddenly finds herself reunited with her childhood "imaginary" friends, who needs her to help them plot against the unseelie court and win the freedom of the faeries.<br><br><u>
  <b>Narrative</b>
</u><br>It was <i>painful</i>. It's like listening to a child with ADHD jumping from one thing to the next. Everything seemed so rushed that you don't get a single connection to the story.<br><br>First example of it popped up right there in the freaking prologue.<br><blockquote>Frank, Stepping Razor's drummer, grabbed Lloyd's arm. Lloyd had just enough time to punch Frank in the face before other patrons tackled him and somebody called the police.<br>By the time the cops got there, Lloyd couldn't remember anything. He was mad as hell, though, cursing Ellen at the top of his lungs. The police drove Kaye and her mother to Lloyd's apartment and waited while Kaye packed their clothes and stuff into plastic garbage bags. Ellen was on the phone, trying to find a place for them to crash.<br>"Honey," Ellen said finally, "we're going to have to go to Grandma's."</blockquote><br><br>So a bit of background info, that's the scene where Lloyd, the dude Kaye's mum is dating, the dude they live with -- tried to kill Kaye's mum. And that is literally the single paragraph where it is mentioned. <br>I don't know about you, but if my boyfriend suddenly lost his marbles and tried to kill me, I'd be in a state of hysteria. I'd be wondering what the flying fook was that all about?!? I'd be dedicating at least an extra paragraph or two to explore the psychological damage that's done me, and probably wrap things up a little smoothly.<br>But nope; not this. Apparently they're happy with <b>"We're going to have to go to grandma's."</b> <br>and the next scene, they're living with Nana and Kaye's off to some rave like some whacko never tried to gut her mama. <a href="http://www.smileycodes.info" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380357927ra/709126.gif" width="72" height="48" alt="http://www.smileycodes.info" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> Like wtf is wrong with you people?!<br><br>And this sort of thing continues persistently throughout the rest of the book. I guess what I'm trying to say is the narrative came out as choppy and rushed; it was emotionally detached from the readers, like an exposition of events. <i>This</i> was happening, and then <i>this</i>, <i>this</i> followed by a whopping amount of <i>this</i>.<br><br><u>
  <b>Characters</b>
</u><br>And this is the second reason why I simply couldn't like <i>Tithe</i>. I just couldn't relate - or even respect - any of them.<br><br>I'm sorry, <b>Black</b>, was I supposed to root for Kaye and her friends? Was I supposed to <i>care</i> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when Janet died <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>??<br><br>So here's the thing. <b>Black</b> was trying to make it seem like Grandma was the annoying, self-righteous, imposing old woman butting into her daughter &amp; grand-daughter's business; and we were supposed to hate her. For shame, Granny, you should know that school is for wussies and you don't <i>need</i> an education for a decent future. Look at your own daughter Ellen! You tried to bring her up with your strict rules and educayshen but she turned out some groupie whore/rockstar wannabe ... better let HER make the decisions for Kaye; she is, after all, her mother. And mother knows best, right? Right??<br><br>Also, the depiction of these ... urban (?) teens really frustrated me. It seems that all they do is get stoned, drink, rave, oh and shoplift. And yes I <i>am</i> aware that some people <i>do</i> do this nonstop and burn their pretty little brain cells away, but if you want to make characters with these traits and no redeeming qualities whatsoever, please don't expect me to care about them.<br><br>Oh and what's with the lack of parental figures in YA? Alright, in this case, what's with the lack of *significant* parental figure? It's like the author wrote Ellen that way just so she conveniently butts out of her daughter's business and doesn't get in the way of her adventure.<br><br><blockquote>Kaye shook her head. It was kind of stupid to think that her mother would just give up on going back to the city, but she couldn't help hoping. "Tell Grandma I won't be home late."<br>"You come home when you want. I'm your mother."</blockquote><br><br><a href="http://www.smileycodes.info" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380357927ra/709127.gif" width="70" height="50" alt="http://www.smileycodes.info" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> ....yes, yes you are.<br><br>So she comes home at like, three in the morning and all's dandy at breakfast the next day. Man am I glad *my* parents weren't that lenient and actually cared if I came home raped or not.<br><br><u>((sidenote))</u> I don't understand why Kaye was made half-Japanese? Is this somehow relevant in the next installments? --cuz it dang well wasn't in this one! --or is it just some odd otaku homage?<span>[image error]</span><br><br><br><u>
  <b>Romance</b>
</u><br>This is the problem with most YAs. I just don't see how these two characters could fall for each other - especially in such short amount of time. Kaye saw Roiben once and fell instantaneously in love with his ... hair? I have no idea. By the way, she met him, bleeding in the woods and her first sentence was <b>"You're a fairie, aren't you?"</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380357927i/709129.png" alt="...and what if I am?" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>...and what if I am?</i><br><br>I also don't know what Roiben sees in Kaye. Apparently she's <b>"Kind, lovely and terribly, terribly brave."</b> I'm not sure about the kind part, just read over the times she lets her best friend's boyfriend feel her up (twice!), get caught, and just run away (both times!) without bothering to see if her "bff" was fine or not.<span>[image error]</span> <br><br>I'm going to go now because everything's a jumble in my head and I have no idea how to put it in a coherent structure. Final word is, I will not be reading the sequels.<br><br><br><br>***<br><i>you can also find reviews at my blog</i><br><a href="http://elfswood.blogspot.com" target="_self" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380227351i/681256.jpg" width="180" alt="elfswood" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15103803975263501186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1944891432" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1944891432" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1944891432?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780689849244" href="/book/show/283495.Tithe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1944891432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18010497976828708461">Holly Black’s writing was my first introduction to fae fiction; as a kid, I was obsessed with all sorts of fae mythology, but typically was limited to nonfiction until the first time I saw <i>Tithe</i> on the “new” shelf at my library. I must have checked this book out and reread it four or five times within the first couple of years, but this was my first reread since I was a preteen, and I had no idea what to expect!<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>If curiosity killed the cat, it was satisfaction that brought it back.</i>
</blockquote><br/>I had forgo</span>
  <span id="freeText18010497976828708461" style="display:none">Holly Black’s writing was my first introduction to fae fiction; as a kid, I was obsessed with all sorts of fae mythology, but typically was limited to nonfiction until the first time I saw <i>Tithe</i> on the “new” shelf at my library. I must have checked this book out and reread it four or five times within the first couple of years, but this was my first reread since I was a preteen, and I had no idea what to expect!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>If curiosity killed the cat, it was satisfaction that brought it back.</i>
</blockquote><br />I had forgotten so much of the plot in this book, and the first thing that surprised me upon rereading it was actually how problematic some of the writing is! If you’re a newer fan of Holly’s and haven’t read her old work, here’s your warning: this book involves racist remarks, homophobic slurs, attempted sexual assault, and some potentially sleazy romance dynamics, most of this going entirely unchallenged as the story unfolds. After one character tries to assault the protagonist, there are even one or two instances in which she talks about feeling flattered by his refusal to take “no” for an answer.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> “And if I said nothing at all?”<br />“Then I would point out that sometimes, if you look at something out of the corner of your eye, you can see right through glamour.”</i>
</blockquote><br />On a more positive note, I had also forgotten how totally addicting the storyline is, how fun and gothic the aesthetic feels, and how lovable Roiben is. While I stand by the fact that the blossoming romance has potential to be problematic, it genuinely doesn’t <i>feel</i> as though Kaye is taking advantage of him with her power over his name. Everything comes across as fully consensual, albeit quite a bit rushed and insta-lovey.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> “I am your servant,” the King of the Unseelie Court said, his lips a moment from her own. “Consider it done.”</i>
</blockquote><br />More than anything, though, I just love the way Holly crafts her fae worlds. Unlike most of today’s popular fae writers, she stays true to the old folklore in many prominent fashions, and my favorite aspect of that is the way she weaves in different types of feyfolk (like sprites, pixies, kelpies, etc.). I have always said that I think Holly is almost singlehandedly responsible for the world of fae YA fiction that so many of us now know and love, and after reading <i>Tithe,</i> despite its imperfections, I adamantly stand by that belief.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18010497976828708461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17294874450318228594">I used to be ridiculously anti-social at family parties and hide out with this book. TITHE was so formative for me as a writer. Unapologetic and gorgeous. TITHE tore off the wings of fairytales and gave them fangs, claws and thorns. I wanted to be Kaye so badly I'd sometimes wander around in my backyard looking for a wounded elf prince. Sadly, no paranormal paramour for me. Although I did date a boy with werewolf sideburns. (I still am, but his sideburns have lost their lycanthropic enthusiasm).</span>

<div id="review_3179803460" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3179803460" />
    <a title="Faith M ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29390149-faith-m"><img alt="Faith M ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587515873p2/29390149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3179803460?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faith M ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faith M ✨" href="/user/show/29390149-faith-m">Faith M ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=butt-ugly-covers">butt-ugly-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=mc-gurl">mc-gurl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=3rd-person">3rd-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=mc-boi">mc-boi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=faeries">faeries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3179803460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7931900009295557708">I wasn’t originally planning on rating this, since I was reading off the omnibus edition released somewhat recently. But oh my goodness, that version changed so much! I’ll go more into that when I review the edition as a whole, but suffice it to say that there was some serious editing that happened between this original version and the combined copy. It’s not just an omnibus, it’s a veritable rewrite.<br/><br/>That said, this was sort of hard to rate even on its own merits. It felt very much like somethin</span>
  <span id="freeText7931900009295557708" style="display:none">I wasn’t originally planning on rating this, since I was reading off the omnibus edition released somewhat recently. But oh my goodness, that version changed so much! I’ll go more into that when I review the edition as a whole, but suffice it to say that there was some serious editing that happened between this original version and the combined copy. It’s not just an omnibus, it’s a veritable rewrite.<br /><br />That said, this was sort of hard to rate even on its own merits. It felt very much like something that I would have been in love with had I read it when I was 13 and utterly obsessed with all things fae. I used to read creepy stories from the 1800s about changelings <i>for fun</i>. And this definitely had those creepy faeries I so craved. I also really liked how the characters were kind of all awful people as that was a great element to add to the intended realism of the story. People are multidimensional and sometimes they’re not rainbows and sunshine all the time. Sometimes a mean protagonist works (I’m looking at you, rewritten Corny 👀)<br /><br />Now, simply having some degree of depth didn’t save this book. It suffered from a truly dreadful plot that was consistently confusing. There were very few clear transitions, so I often had no idea what was even happening and when it occurred. And from what I did understand, this had nothing to say. It was largely pointless. It dallied with some themes but didn’t stick with them in any meaningful way. I find Black’s work tends to do this often. I’ve never read something by her that had anything to it. It’s all aesthetic for aesthetic’s sake, which is fine, I guess, but undeniably boring after a while.<br /><br />Though I will say, she’s the only urban fantasy author who doesn’t irk me with unnecessary real world insertion. She lets the fantasy feel plausible enough on its own without making grand claims about how Harry Houdini was a demigod 😒🙄 One way to break reality is to bring up reality, and she didn’t do that. She just wrote a world like our own and put spooky faeries in it. So good job, I guess!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7931900009295557708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_68582893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68582893" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/68582893?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68582893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18152234757662194582">"Tithe: A Modern Faerie Tale" is about sixteen year old Kaye Fierch, a girl who has been moving around with her single mother for her entire life. At a young age she has been able to see and interact with these things called faeries, although no one believed her. Then one day, she enchants a boy into falling in love with her and makes a broken, splintered horse move. Soon after that event she meets a young faerie night named Roiben, and that is just the start of her faerie adventure.<br/><br/>Hm... okay, </span>
  <span id="freeText18152234757662194582" style="display:none">"Tithe: A Modern Faerie Tale" is about sixteen year old Kaye Fierch, a girl who has been moving around with her single mother for her entire life. At a young age she has been able to see and interact with these things called faeries, although no one believed her. Then one day, she enchants a boy into falling in love with her and makes a broken, splintered horse move. Soon after that event she meets a young faerie night named Roiben, and that is just the start of her faerie adventure.<br /><br />Hm... okay, the reason I picked up this book was because I heard that it had a gay side character. On that note, this character, Corny, was absolutely underdeveloped. In fact, almost all of the side characters were underdeveloped, I felt like I didn't know a single thing about any of them. This book also feels like it moves from event to event, but not with the grace or ability that a good author has to string her storyline together. <br /><br />There were some scenes that were just plain difficult to read. Some examples are when Kaye told Robien to "kiss her ass", and Robien actually did because he was "bound" to her. If Robien was bound to do what Kaye demanded of him, then I think Robien would've understood that what Kaye demanded of him wasn't the literal sense of what she said, but the emotional sense. Also, there was a scene where Corny is in the underground faerie hill with this strange prince character, and then Corny is tortured. Like, he is completely helpless and starts eating everything he can get his hands on. A rotten apple. The dirt on the ground. And some ants. For Pete's sake, when I read that, I thought I was going to be sick. And what's even weirder is that NO ONE even CARED about what happened to him. In fact, the only thing in the book that acknowledges that the event occurred is when Corny starts blindly stabbing his tormentor to death. Which was a total "huh?" moment to me.<br /><br />This is the first book I have deemed worthy of one star. Totally disappointing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18152234757662194582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chan ☆" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chan ☆" href="/user/show/48727754-chan">chan ☆</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1516050647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12479180365730774978"><b>“What’s next on the faerie agenda?”<br/>“I get sacrificed, I guess.”<br/>“Great. When is that?”</b><br/><br/>oh, holly black. you never cease to make me laugh, gasp, and shake my head. this book was no exception, and for a debut novel (WRITTEN IN 2002!!!) no less.<br/><br/>book follows a girl named kaye who has always thought the world had a little magic. after moving back to her hometown and saving an injured fae knight, she figures out that she's right. she also discovers there might be a little more to her personal history th</span>
  <span id="freeText12479180365730774978" style="display:none"><b>“What’s next on the faerie agenda?”<br />“I get sacrificed, I guess.”<br />“Great. When is that?”</b><br /><br />oh, holly black. you never cease to make me laugh, gasp, and shake my head. this book was no exception, and for a debut novel (WRITTEN IN 2002!!!) no less.<br /><br />book follows a girl named kaye who has always thought the world had a little magic. after moving back to her hometown and saving an injured fae knight, she figures out that she's right. she also discovers there might be a little more to her personal history than she thought &amp; she is grappling with this while trying to avoid being used as a human sacrifice.<br /><br />heavy stuff. sort of. the atmosphere of this book is unlike that of the cruel prince. it's almost a complete reversal: instead of a human growing up in a fae you have a non-human growing up in the human world. and i think that's why this was a little bit bumpy.<br /><br />almost half of the book is spent in the real world while kaye is dealing with her shitty mom, and some random side characters. i know it's meant to slowly introduce magic back into kaye's world but it sort of bored me. <br /><br />thankfully the characters and their relationships made up for that. the vibes that i got from kaye &amp; roiben (aforementioned fae knight) were very jude and cardan-esque. not quite the same enemies to lovers relationship but i was seriously DYING for them to hook up. which was just as i remembered from my read of this in middle school. lol.<br /><br />i'm giving this 3 stars because it felt nostalgic and for the time it was written it was insanely inventive and dark. but the plot was a little confusing and wrapped up a little too neatly at the end for my taste. <b>i think this just shows how much holly has grown as an author.</b> and i'm still going to read the other 2 books. i'm trash for angst.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_17160067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17160067" />
    <a title="Juushika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/616321-juushika"><img alt="Juushika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541586729p2/616321.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17160067?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juushika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juushika" href="/user/show/616321-juushika">Juushika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=status-borrowed">status-borrowed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17160067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1991484700899441402">As a child, Kaye had faery friends; throughout her life, she has always been unusual. Now, following an barfight, Kaye and her would-be-rock star mother return to Kaye's childhood home. There, Kaye meets another faery, and discovers that her childhood friends really do exist and that she is far more unusual than she ever suspected. She soon falls into the middle of the power struggle between two rival faery courts, a struggle which could easily spill into the human world. <i>Tithe</i> is a mix of wonde</span>
  <span id="freeText1991484700899441402" style="display:none">As a child, Kaye had faery friends; throughout her life, she has always been unusual. Now, following an barfight, Kaye and her would-be-rock star mother return to Kaye's childhood home. There, Kaye meets another faery, and discovers that her childhood friends really do exist and that she is far more unusual than she ever suspected. She soon falls into the middle of the power struggle between two rival faery courts, a struggle which could easily spill into the human world. <i>Tithe</i> is a mix of wonderful and horrible aspects: the characters are difficult to like or identify with, and the writing style is inconsistent and immature, but the plot is realistically complex (even though it ends abruptly) and the faeries are dark, enthralling, and vividly conceived (if overdrawn). I found this book at times both frustrating and wonderful, and though it has many faults, I still recommend it for its plot and atmosphere, as well as its great potential.<br /><br />At the beginning of reading <i>Tithe</i>, the weaknesses far outweigh the strengths. Kaye, her mother, and her friends are neither likable nor identifiableKaye's mother is a struggling rock vocalist, Kaye is a high school drop out, Janet is a superficial teenager, Corny is an unattractive gas station attendant; everyone drinks too much and smokes too much. Maybe I just lived a sheltered life, but wouldn't have identified with any of these characters as a young adult, and I still don't now as an adult. They are not likable, nor are their flaws realisticinstead, they are exaggerated and simplistic. Along with difficult characterization, the writing style is inconsistent and immature, replete with adverbs, repeated gestures, and dull dialog and episodes. This is clearly a first novel, and accordingly it feels unfinished and unpolished. The book would have benefited from a rewrite, to tighten the language and unify the style.<br /><br />But for all of these negative qualities, <i>Tithe</i> remains readable and exhibits some real jewels and true potential as it goes on. The plot moves just fast enough that it is not frustrating and slow enough that it is still intriguing. There are many points where the book could have ended prematurely, wrapping up the plot into a nice and neat package; Black, however, rejects these endings, instead introducing new complications to build a plot that is is political, complex, and ongoing. The unfortunate effect of the ongoing story is that the book has an indistinct endingalthough not a cliffhanger, it seems arbitrary and incomplete. On the whole, however, the complex plot fits the book's wide political premise and makes for a satisfying read. The faeries are equally satisfying: they are otherworldly, diverse, and carefully imagined. Some of the dark faeries are overdrawn and excessively macabre, but on the whole the faeries are the highlight of the text. Black's imagination is lively and wide; her descriptions (in particular Kaye's transformation) shine off of the page in vivid language that is at once ethereal and tactile.<br /><br />I found this to be an alternately frustrating and delightful book. The characters disappointed me, the writing style annoyed me, but whenever I became too frustrated, another new aspect would shine: a banquet scene in a faery court, a new plot development, some measure of character growth. So while I can't rate this book very highly on account of its many faults, I do recommend it. Less critical readers may not find it so frustrating as I did; no matter the reader, the magic and imagination make this a book worth reading. There is great potential here, and where it is realized, <i>Tithe</i> is a truly enjoyable read. I look forward to reading more of Black's published workI expect that as she matured as a writer, her books became more readable and less frustrating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1991484700899441402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53113267" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/653329-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1196562214p2/653329.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53113267?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/653329-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53113267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3747629252895756710">I ended up reading this book by accident. It was recommended to my 14 year old, Gini. She began the book and then brought it to me saying that she didn't feel it was appropriate for kids and that she, personally, had no interest in a heroine who consistently made such poor life choices. Well! I decided to read it to see what the deal was. This book was recommended for kids 14 and up and Gini has read books that were definitely adult reading level and she LOVES faery. <br/><br/>The problem with this book f</span>
  <span id="freeText3747629252895756710" style="display:none">I ended up reading this book by accident. It was recommended to my 14 year old, Gini. She began the book and then brought it to me saying that she didn't feel it was appropriate for kids and that she, personally, had no interest in a heroine who consistently made such poor life choices. Well! I decided to read it to see what the deal was. This book was recommended for kids 14 and up and Gini has read books that were definitely adult reading level and she LOVES faery. <br /><br />The problem with this book for Gini (and I am proud of her for it) is that the girl, Kaye, who is the main character, as well as her friends, smoke, drink, sneak around, fool around, and generally make all the choices that parents hope their children will avoid. Gini loves books and movies with really strong female characters. Ultraviolet, Alias, Charmed, Dragonlance, Bones and Sarah Connor Chronicles are some of her favorites. She just really didn't like the idea that a 16 year old who was so "messed up" and misguided would be turned into a heroine of faery. She appreciates that the best heroines have flaws to overcome but this just didn't work for her.<br /><br />Now! All that that being said, I finished the book and for an adult with the grace of age and perspective, this book is a fun, light read. This poor kid who has pretty much raised herself and her mother could very well end up the same dead-end mess that her mother has but she doesn't. She discovers something very special within herself. She ends up showing a lot of character and courage. The teens dealt with in the book are not the teens that I have guided my girls to become or to identify with but those kids are out there and they have the same potential and beauty within them. It was really cool to talk to Gini about why she didn't like this character and how the character developed without requiring her to read something she objected to and without glorifying the type of kid portrayed in the book. <br /><br />This is just my opinion folks so take it for what it is worth to you! I would not have this book in the hands of anyone under 16 and even at 16, my girls would probably not read this type of material if for no other reason than the frequency of the "f" word which we don't appreciate in our home, hearts or heads and the underage drinking and sexuality. But if you do have a child who wants to read it and you don't like to censor your child's reading (and I do very little of that, believe it or not - I teach them the principles and let them apply them, which Gini did very well) then this book is a good opportunity to talk about the choices the kids in the book make. Why it may or may not be a good idea for an author to portray a young person with such poor judgement as a hero or heroine (I thought it was a great idea!) and how people can turn their lives around no matter how dismal and dead-end they seem to be.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3747629252895756710" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2629010335" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2629010335" />
    <a title="Amy Imogene Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84702001-amy-imogene-reads"><img alt="Amy Imogene Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548082309p2/84702001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Imogene Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Imogene Reads" href="/user/show/84702001-amy-imogene-reads">Amy Imogene Reads</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2629010335" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7921611773797999404">2.75 stars<br/><br/>Alright y'all, take this review with a grain of salt because I'm sucker for Holly Black. I liked this because it was Holly Black, faeries, and drama. Was it amazing? Nope. Did I enjoy it though? Oh yeah. <br/><br/><b>Concept:</b> ★★★<br/><b>Plot:</b> ★★<br/><b>Enjoyment:</b> ★★★★ (so sue me, I love any and all things Fae and under the mound)<br/><br/>Keeping this review SUPER short and sweet because there's not much to say about this book with spoiling it and/or getting way too involved in a larger discussion on the tropes of early 200</span>
  <span id="freeText7921611773797999404" style="display:none">2.75 stars<br /><br />Alright y'all, take this review with a grain of salt because I'm sucker for Holly Black. I liked this because it was Holly Black, faeries, and drama. Was it amazing? Nope. Did I enjoy it though? Oh yeah. <br /><br /><b>Concept:</b> ★★★<br /><b>Plot:</b> ★★<br /><b>Enjoyment:</b> ★★★★ (so sue me, I love any and all things Fae and under the mound)<br /><br />Keeping this review SUPER short and sweet because there's not much to say about this book with spoiling it and/or getting way too involved in a larger discussion on the tropes of early 2000s YA fantasy. <br /><br /><i>Tithe</i> is one of Holly Black's earliest novels, and I don't think it's a bad thing to say that it reads that way. Every author starts somewhere. <b>This was a solid series opener considering the time it was published, the tropes at play in that era, and the concepts of faerie/Fae that were being developed in the YA scene</b> in the realm of "real world" and "urban fantasy meets faeries"—which Holly Black had a major hand in forming, along with Melissa Marr and few others. I was trash for that trope then and I'm trash for it now. (Who doesn't want to be walking down the street one day and see a faerie???)<br /><br />One of the interesting elements of <i>Tithe</i> was how many concepts were clearly rough blueprints for her Cruel Prince trilogy. It's not a direct comparison—which is good—but the bones are there. And in some cases, that is literal: <b>Roiben and Faye, the two protagonists in <i>Tithe</i>, are actually IN <i>The Cruel Prince</i> as distanced minor characters.</b> Once I'm done with this series, I'll probably revisit The Cruel Prince to see how her timelines line up.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.amyimogenereads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/amyimogenereads/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7921611773797999404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1953266602" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1953266602" />
    <a title="Chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33012180-chelsea"><img alt="Chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537582300p2/33012180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1953266602?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/33012180-chelsea">Chelsea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33012180-chelsea?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1953266602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13701227503121845624"><b>
  <u>Series Review</u>
</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe__Modern_Faerie_Tales___1_' title='Tithe (Modern Faerie Tales, #1) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tithe</a>: 3 stars<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/266607.Valiant__Modern_Faerie_Tales__2_' title='Valiant (Modern Faerie Tales #2) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Valiant</a>: 2 stars (barely)<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/283494.Ironside__Modern_Faerie_Tales___3_' title='Ironside (Modern Faerie Tales, #3) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ironside</a>: 3 1/2 stars<br/><br/><b>I am a huge fan of Holly Black, specifically her writing style. Both <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20958632.The_Darkest_Part_of_the_Forest' title='The Darkest Part of the Forest by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Darkest Part of the Forest</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12813630.The_Coldest_Girl_in_Coldtown' title='The Coldest Girl in Coldtown by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</a> were five star books for me</b>, and this is coming from someone who typically gets bored by fantasy after a chapter or two.<br/><br/><b>There’s something about Holly Black’s writing style that is so lovely and dark and perfectly fitting for the stories she tells.</b><br/><br/>With the release of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26032825.The_Cruel_Prince__The_Folk_of_the_Air___1_' title='The Cruel Prince (The Folk of the Air, #1) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Cruel Prince</a>, which</span>
  <span id="freeText13701227503121845624" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Series Review</u>
</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe__Modern_Faerie_Tales___1_" title="Tithe (Modern Faerie Tales, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Tithe</a>: 3 stars<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/266607.Valiant__Modern_Faerie_Tales__2_" title="Valiant (Modern Faerie Tales #2) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Valiant</a>: 2 stars (barely)<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/283494.Ironside__Modern_Faerie_Tales___3_" title="Ironside (Modern Faerie Tales, #3) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Ironside</a>: 3 1/2 stars<br /><br /><b>I am a huge fan of Holly Black, specifically her writing style. Both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20958632.The_Darkest_Part_of_the_Forest" title="The Darkest Part of the Forest by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">The Darkest Part of the Forest</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12813630.The_Coldest_Girl_in_Coldtown" title="The Coldest Girl in Coldtown by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</a> were five star books for me</b>, and this is coming from someone who typically gets bored by fantasy after a chapter or two.<br /><br /><b>There’s something about Holly Black’s writing style that is so lovely and dark and perfectly fitting for the stories she tells.</b><br /><br />With the release of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26032825.The_Cruel_Prince__The_Folk_of_the_Air___1_" title="The Cruel Prince (The Folk of the Air, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cruel Prince</a>, which is getting a ridiculous amount of hype right now, I decided I wanted to read Black’s original fae trilogy, more out of curiosity than anything else.<br /><br /><b>As someone used to reading more polished works from this author, going back to her debut was a bit underwhelming, though it makes sense.</b> There’s going to be a gap in quality between a book published in 2002 and one published in 2018.<br /><br />Let’s reflect on the fact that this series was first published in 2002. Damn, that’s early for YA novels - pre-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> and pre-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>. <b>Holly Black wrote a paranormal romance before paranormal romances were even a thing.</b><br /><br />Here’s a crazy part: <b>this book is one of the more diverse fantasy series I’ve read. AND IT WAS PUBLISHED IN 2002.</b> I really don’t want to hear excuses about how early YA series couldn’t have diverse characters - <b>this one (which is actually pretty popular and published by a major publishing house) had a main character who is mixed race (white and Japanese) and an explicitly gay main character who has a romantic plotline in the final book.</b><br /><br />The book itself has a lot of room to grow, which Black did as she continued to publish books. <b>It’s entertaining and has seeds of the lyrical prose I have come to expect from Black, but it’s just not...great.</b><br /><br /><b>Tithe</b>: I mean, <b>I was expecting more of a dark fairytale, so I’ll admit I was a bit disappointed when this ended up being more in the vein of paranormal romance.</b> It has a lot of the hallmarks of the starts to early YA fantasy series, but the writing is bit better than those books usually are.<br /><br /><b>Valiant</b>: Why was this book even a thing? It was like this random companion novel that had no impact on the series. And it was boring. <b>I wish I’d skipped it.</b><br /><br /><b>Ironside:</b> Definitely the best of the three. The most entertaining, some cool plot stuff, character development, writing improvement. Almost made the whole series worth it!<br /><br />Overall, I probably wouldn’t recommend this series. Holly Black has books that are so much better, and I wouldn’t waste my time with these unless I’m a really diehard fan. <b>I’m even more excited to tackle <i>The Cruel Prince</i> now - I can’t wait to see how Holly Black writes faeries 16 years after her first faerie novel was published!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13701227503121845624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"><img alt=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529467844p2/703854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=own-physical-copy">own-physical-copy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer217756172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4590052673642559148">This was so much fun! I started out very unsure about it, since it was recommended to me by a The Iron Fey fan, I was expecting something else. But Tithe is far darker than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6644117.The_Iron_King__The_Iron_Fey___1_' title='The Iron King (The Iron Fey, #1) by Julie Kagawa' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Iron King</a>. It was very thematic and I was thrown off by the heroine's heavy drinking, smoking, swearing, and shoplifting, a girl of 16. But once I got acquainted with its world different is not necessarily bad.<br/><br/>Kaye attracts the attention of a gorgeous fey of the Unseelie Court, a knight. Roiben has the whole victim-of-cir</span>
  <span id="freeText4590052673642559148" style="display:none">This was so much fun! I started out very unsure about it, since it was recommended to me by a The Iron Fey fan, I was expecting something else. But Tithe is far darker than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6644117.The_Iron_King__The_Iron_Fey___1_" title="The Iron King (The Iron Fey, #1) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron King</a>. It was very thematic and I was thrown off by the heroine's heavy drinking, smoking, swearing, and shoplifting, a girl of 16. But once I got acquainted with its world different is not necessarily bad.<br /><br />Kaye attracts the attention of a gorgeous fey of the Unseelie Court, a knight. Roiben has the whole victim-of-circumstances vibe down, but I was actually a little scared of Roiben in the beginning. He seemed so evil and menacing. I was hesitant to start liking him, but eventually I couldn't resist him anymore! The romance was well played out, better than some YA. But I don't know if anything will ever beat The Iron Fey in my mind.<br /><br />Being only my second faerie series, it was interesting to see the similarities and differences from The Iron Fey. I was not previously familiar with ideas of faerie glamour, and the courts, and I didnt know how much was unique to The Iron Fey. So that was interesting and I now have a better grasp of it. I found the story very interesting and exciting with a lot of twists and turns. But the very best part is the ending! It ended on such a great note I couldn't stop giggling.<br /><br />The ending. <i>THE ENDING!</i> Hehehe, awesome!</span>

<div id="review_1470915962" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1470915962" />
    <a title="Lia  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48295288-lia"><img alt="Lia  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594824825p2/48295288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1470915962?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lia  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lia  " href="/user/show/48295288-lia">Lia  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=english-and-american-lit-and-more">english-and-american-lit-and-more</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=magic-and-supernatural-things">magic-and-supernatural-things</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=fairies-and-the-fae-world">fairies-and-the-fae-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1470915962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16822476673757618521"><u>3.25 stars</u><br/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Half the fun's in lies we tell ourselves.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>My favorite thing about faerie books is always their eerie atmosphere. I don't mind gory horror, but what I truly love is that creepy feeling I get with mysterious and intriguing books like this one. And while <i>Tithe</i> did not leave me in awe, it was still very well-written, and it kept me hooked from beginning to end. <br/><br/>Holly Black is one of my favorite fantasy authors. She wrote The Curse Workers trilogy, my favorite urban fantasy series of all</span>
  <span id="freeText16822476673757618521" style="display:none"><u>3.25 stars</u><br /><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Half the fun's in lies we tell ourselves.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br />My favorite thing about faerie books is always their eerie atmosphere. I don't mind gory horror, but what I truly love is that creepy feeling I get with mysterious and intriguing books like this one. And while <i>Tithe</i> did not leave me in awe, it was still very well-written, and it kept me hooked from beginning to end. <br /><br />Holly Black is one of my favorite fantasy authors. She wrote The Curse Workers trilogy, my favorite urban fantasy series of all time, but I also knew she had written this book twelve years ago, and I've always thought that most (not all) authors are a bit like wine: they get better as time passes. So I was not expecting anything nearly as good as The Curse Workers, but this book still managed to surprise me.<br />It surely had a lot of clichés of the genre - some insta-love, a quirky sidekick like Corny (even though his storyline quickly took an unexpected darker turn) and mostly forgettable secondary characters.<br />However, not only the writing was very good (there were a couple of metaphors that really took my breath away), but this book was <b>dark.</b> Extremely dark for a YA book. In fact, I would not recommend it to younger teens at all, but I appreciated this new kind of perspective immensely. Teenagers in this book are not the goody two-shoes we're used to, the usual perfect kids that never do anything wrong. These teenagers drink, smoke, party and have sex. They have difficult relationships with their families and with each other, they swear and they lie, and they usually result much more realistic than your average YA characters. <br /><br />I will soon read the second and third book in the series, because this was an interesting start and, although somehow flawed, it was also something new and unexpected that I want to see more of. The plot may be a bit basic, but Holly's portrayal of the fae world is not. I was particularly impressed by the way she described the Unseelie Court, a place of viciousness and pleasure and pain - and its inhabitants weren't any different. It was intriguing, and dangerous. They all were. <br />As for the characters, I did not care too much for any of them, but I was fascinated by the unconventional main character, Kaye, and her dysfunctional family, and I can't wait to know what's going to happen to Corny, Kaye's human friend who forgot common sense and delved a little too deep into the faerie courts. <i>Tithe</i> was a good book, and despite the things I did not like about it, it was definitely <i>not</i> average. And even though it's one of Holly's early works, I know she will still somehow manage to surprise me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16822476673757618521" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28683811-noura-khalid-theperksofbeingnoura?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,
